                                                                                      Convert flat $0.30 customer support to phase-basedBalraj / ClaudeMedium
                                                                                      Add Fixed Monthly Burn section (founder salary, legal, insurance)Balraj / ClaudeMedium
                                                                                      Validate iOS payment routing — Stripe-first vs Apple IAPBalraj (tech)Medium
                                                                                      Lock final retail prices for India/Brazil/Africa zonal pricing (v1.1)Balraj / AkitoLow (3-6mo post-launch)

                                                                                      PART II — Tab 2: User Behavior

                                                                                      Tab 2 is the intelligence layer of the P&L model — it predicts how much data crew will actually USE (not buy). Every downstream tab references this to compute COGS, gross margin, LTV, and breakage. We pay our supplier per GB consumed, not per GB sold — so predicting consumption accurately is the difference between profitable and unprofitable.
                                                                                      Tab 2 — Table of Contents
                                                                                      • 1. What Tab 2 does and why it matters
                                                                                      • 2. The 4 user archetypes (Light / Average / Heavy / Churner)
                                                                                      • 3. Per-tier consumption — the real driver
                                                                                      • 4. The 1-GB refill UX (the key insight)
                                                                                      • 5. Breakage column — where profit appears
                                                                                      • 6. How Tab 2 feeds the rest of the model
                                                                                      • 7. Validation queue
                                                                                      • 8. Ethics — transparency-first breakage

                                                                                      1. What Tab 2 does and why it matters

                                                                                      Tab 2 answers one question:

                                                                                      Given that a crew member buys a plan, how much data will they actually use — and how often will they refuel?

                                                                                      This single prediction drives every downstream tab. We pay our supplier per GB consumed, not per GB sold. So predicting consumption accurately is the difference between profitable and unprofitable.

                                                                                      The tab has two layers:

                                                                                      LayerWhat it does
                                                                                      Layer 1 — ArchetypesDefines 4 generic user types (Light / Average / Heavy / Churner) with their consumption + refuel attach rates. Conceptual model.
                                                                                      Layer 2 — Per-tier consumptionApplies tier-specific consumption rates that override the archetype weighted average. The actual driver of COGS.

                                                                                      2. The 4 user archetypes

                                                                                      Every paying crew member falls into one of four buckets, regardless of tier:

                                                                                      Archetype% of users% pool consumedRefuel attachMental picture
                                                                                      Light25%30%10%"Subscribed Premium just in case." Pool sits mostly unused. The profit-engine cohort.
                                                                                      Average40%65%30%Default crew. Eats most of pool. Refuels ~1 month in 3.
                                                                                      Heavy30%95%65%Long-haul + connectivity dependent. Almost full consumption, often refuels.
                                                                                      Churner5%10%0%Tries one month, cancels. Single-month pure breakage.

                                                                                      Why crew-skewed (25/40/30/5) instead of general (40/35/20/5)

                                                                                      Crew fly 8-12 layovers/month as their job. They're heavier travelers than vacationers. The bell curve shifts right. We're modeling truck drivers, not weekend tourists.

                                                                                      Confidence: Estimate — the 25/40/30/5 shift is logical but not validated by crew-specific data. Original 40/35/20/5 is grounded in general SaaS benchmarks (RevenueCat, ProfitWell, OpenView).

                                                                                      3. Per-tier consumption — the real driver

                                                                                      After we locked the 1-GB refill UX, the single weighted average from archetypes no longer reflected reality. Friction makes a Premium user behave differently than a First Suite user even when they're both "Average."

                                                                                      So we replaced the single weighted average with per-tier rates:

                                                                                      TierPool% ConsumedGB ConsumedReasoning
                                                                                      Economy (PAYG)1 GB100%1 GBBuy what you need, consume what you buy
                                                                                      Roster Bundle5 flights100%5 SIMsPer-flight, each used on that trip
                                                                                      Premium Economy10 GB40%4 GBSmall pool, 1-GB friction caps usage
                                                                                      Business ⭐15 GB45%6.75 GBSlightly heavier users, same friction
                                                                                      First25 GB54%13.5 GBHeavy users push near friction cap
                                                                                      First Suite40 GB33%13.2 GBSame heavy users (~13 GB), big pool dilutes %
                                                                                      Cockpit12 GB60%7.2 GBTight pool, friction less constraining
                                                                                      Refuel1 GB100%1 GBTop-up, consumed on purchase

                                                                                      Confidence: Estimate — these per-tier rates are derived from the friction logic. Real consumption could land 30-70% depending on UX behavior. App analytics months 1-3 post-launch will replace estimates with measured values.

                                                                                      4. The 1-GB refill UX (the key insight)

                                                                                      Users see only 1 GB active at a time. When that GB runs out, they tap "Refill from pool" to get the next GB. The pool is always visible (transparency), but refill requires manual action.

                                                                                      This single design choice produces three compounding effects:

                                                                                      EffectMechanism
                                                                                      Lower consumptionFriction-limited usage drops from ~62.5% to ~40-60% per tier
                                                                                      More breakageUnused pool either carries (deferred breakage) or expires immediately
                                                                                      Pool expansion is freeGoing from 25 GB First to 40 GB First Suite doesn't change COGS — friction still caps usage at ~13 GB. Bigger pool just improves perceived value.

                                                                                      The "pool expansion is free" insight in numbers

                                                                                      TierPoolFriction-capped consumptionPer-GB price
                                                                                      Premium Economy10 GB4 GB (40%)$1.80
                                                                                      Business15 GB6.75 GB (45%)$2.00
                                                                                      First25 GB13.5 GB (54%)$1.60
                                                                                      First Suite ⭐40 GB13.2 GB (33%)$1.25 ← best on ladder

                                                                                      First Suite consumes the same absolute GB as First but with a 60% bigger pool. Same COGS, dramatically better marketing position. That's why First Suite is the anchor product.

                                                                                      5. Breakage column — where profit appears

                                                                                      Breakage = GB the user paid for, but never used. Once it expires (no carryover left), we keep the revenue but never pay our supplier. 100% margin on those GB.

                                                                                      TierPoolConsumedUnusedCarriesImmediate Breakage
                                                                                      Premium Economy10 GB4 GB6 GB3 GB (50%)3 GB ⭐
                                                                                      Business15 GB6.75 GB8.25 GB5.78 GB (70%)2.48 GB
                                                                                      First25 GB13.5 GB11.5 GB11.5 GB (100%)0 GB (deferred)
                                                                                      First Suite40 GB13.2 GB26.8 GB26.8 GB (100%)0 GB (deferred)
                                                                                      Cockpit12 GB7.2 GB4.8 GB4.8 GB (100%)0 GB (deferred)

                                                                                      Why top tiers show ZERO immediate breakage

                                                                                      First, First Suite, and Cockpit all have 100% × 2 month carry. That means month 1 unused rolls forward, doesn't break immediately. Real breakage hits at end of month 2 as carryover ages out.

                                                                                      Tab 10 (Carryover Liability) tracks this aging properly. Tab 2 shows only the monthly snapshot.

                                                                                      Breakage in dollars (Premium Economy example)

                                                                                      3 GB breakage × $1.34 blended wholesale = $4.02 of pure profit per Premium user per month (updated 2026-06-01: blended cost revised from $1.20 to $1.34/GB after geo mix recalibration to 75/20/5).

                                                                                      ScalePremium users (13%)Monthly breakage profitAnnual
                                                                                      10,000 users1,300$5,226$62,712
                                                                                      100,000 users13,000$52,260$627,120

                                                                                      6. How Tab 2 feeds the rest of the model

                                                                                      Tab 2 outputs flow into 7+ downstream tabs:

                                                                                      TabUses Tab 2 for...Produces
                                                                                      Tab 3 — Per-Tier Unit EconomicsGB Consumed → COGS per userGross margin per tier
                                                                                      Tab 4 — Pricing SimulatorBehavior inputsBreak-even / margin-target retail prices
                                                                                      Tab 5 — Volume ScenariosPer-user economics × user counts1K / 5K / 10K / 100K P&L
                                                                                      Tab 7 — Behavior SensitivityArchetype mix (rows 7-11)What-if mix scenarios
                                                                                      Tab 8 — LTV-CAC + ChurnConsumption + churnLifetime value per tier
                                                                                      Tab 10 — Carryover LiabilityGB Carries columnDeferred revenue + aging schedule
                                                                                      Tab 11 — Strategic ScenariosBehavior under different supplier pathsWholesale supplier vs direct comparison
                                                                                      Per-plan Logic tabsPer-tier consumption + behaviorPlan-specific deep-dive economics
                                                                                      Tab 2 is the factory floor. Every other tab is a different report from the same factory. Change ANY number in Tab 2 and the entire workbook recalculates.

                                                                                      7. Validation queue — what needs real data

                                                                                      About half of Tab 2's numbers are educated estimates. The validation queue captures everything that needs to be tested against real data:

                                                                                      Item to validateOwnerWhenStatus
                                                                                      Archetype mix (25/40/30/5 crew-skewed)AkitoThis weekEstimate
                                                                                      Per-archetype consumption % (30/65/95/10)AkitoSame crew interviewsEstimate
                                                                                      Per-archetype refuel attach (10/30/65/0%)AkitoSame crew interviewsEstimate
                                                                                      Per-tier consumption rates (40/45/54/33/60%)App analyticsMonths 1-3 post-launchEstimate
                                                                                      Refuel attach by tier (still uses archetype avg)ClaudeNext passBug to fix
                                                                                      Document Economy/Roster "100% consumption" model abstractionClaudeThis blueprintDone
                                                                                      Add "Source / Confidence" column to Tab 2ClaudeNext passPending

                                                                                      Akito's crew interview script — what to ask

                                                                                      QuestionWhat it validates
                                                                                      "In a typical month, how much of your data plan do you actually use? Most of it? Some? Barely any?"Archetype distribution (Light/Avg/Heavy)
                                                                                      "Do you usually need to buy a top-up before the end of the month?"Refuel attach rate
                                                                                      "When you have extra data left at end of month, does it bother you to lose it?"Carryover sensitivity
                                                                                      "How would you feel about uploading your monthly roster for automatic eSIM activation?"Roster Bundle adoption
                                                                                      "What's the most you'd pay per month for a reliable global travel eSIM?"Price ceiling validation

                                                                                      8. Ethics — transparency-first breakage

                                                                                      Breakage is a real profit lever. But it's only ethical if the user has every chance to consume what they paid for.

                                                                                      Locked transparency ruleWhy
                                                                                      Pool ALWAYS visibleNever hide what user paid for
                                                                                      Refill button visible at all timesOne tap, no hidden friction
                                                                                      Day-25 reminder push notificationGive them every chance to consume
                                                                                      Carryover shown explicitly: "Y GB will carry, Z GB will expire"Honest disclosure
                                                                                      Breakage we earn from honest forgetfulness is fair revenue. Breakage we earn from hidden mechanics is fraud.

                                                                                      This was Balraj's call (2026-06-01). The locked policy means even though the 1-GB refill UX creates more breakage, every user has full visibility and explicit reminders. They can fully utilize their pool if they want to.

                                                                                      PART III — Tab 3: Per-Tier Unit Economics

                                                                                      Tab 3 in one sentence

                                                                                      Tab 3 translates the retail prices from Tab 1 and the consumption behavior from Tab 2 into a single per-USER profit number for each tier. It is the bridge between architecture and money. Every downstream scaling tab (Volume Scenarios, 24-Month Rollout, LTV-CAC) multiplies these per-user numbers by user counts.

                                                                                      Table of Contents — Part III
                                                                                      • 1. Purpose — what Tab 3 does (and what it doesn't)
                                                                                      • 2. The 13 columns explained (3 column groups)
                                                                                      • 3. Per-tier results table (locked numbers)
                                                                                      • 4. Strategic insights — which tier wins, which is weakest
                                                                                      • 5. Downstream consumption — how Tab 3 feeds the rest
                                                                                      • 6. Confidence assessment per input
                                                                                      • 7. Validation queue
                                                                                      • 8. Bite 6 — Sensitivity analysis (what could break us)

                                                                                      1. Purpose — what Tab 3 does (and what it doesn't)

                                                                                      Tab 3 ISTab 3 is NOT
                                                                                      Per-USER math (one subscriber, one month)Total revenue or company-level P&L
                                                                                      The translation layer between Tab 1 (prices) and Tab 2 (behavior) and moneyA scaling tab — multiplication by user counts happens in Tab 5+
                                                                                      Where COGS, gross margin, and net margin are computed for each planA sensitivity tab — that's Tab 7
                                                                                      The source of every "per user / month" number quoted in pitchesA churn or LTV tab — that's Tab 8
                                                                                      If Tab 1 is the menu and Tab 2 is the appetite, Tab 3 is the kitchen receipt. One customer, one meal, one number.

                                                                                      2. The 13 columns explained

                                                                                      Tab 3's 13 columns are organized into three logical groups, each color-coded in the workbook for fast visual parsing.

                                                                                      Group 1 — Inputs Columns A–D (blue)

                                                                                      The four upstream-fed inputs. None of these are calculated in Tab 3 — they pull from Tab 1 and Tab 2.

                                                                                      ColNameSourceExample (Business)
                                                                                      ATier nameTab 1 row labelBusiness ⭐
                                                                                      BMonthly RevenueTab 1 retail price$29.99
                                                                                      CGB ConsumedTab 2 per-tier consumption6.75 GB (45% of 15 GB pool)
                                                                                      DWholesale $/GBTab 1 blended cost ($1.34 at 75/20/5 mix)$1.34/GB

                                                                                      Group 2 — eSIM & Refuel Math Columns E–H (amber)

                                                                                      The four columns that compute the eSIM data cost plus refuel add-on revenue + cost.

                                                                                      ColNameFormulaExample (Business)
                                                                                      EeSIM COGSC × D6.75 × $1.34 = $9.05
                                                                                      FRefuel Attach %Tab 2 per-tier estimate (currently uses 25% for Business)25%
                                                                                      GRefuel RevenueF × $4.99 (refuel price from Tab 1)0.25 × $4.99 = $1.25
                                                                                      HRefuel COGSF × 1 GB × D0.25 × 1 × $1.34 = $0.34

                                                                                      Group 3 — Profit Math Columns I–M (green)

                                                                                      The five columns that roll everything into a single per-user profit number.

                                                                                      ColNameFormulaExample (Business)
                                                                                      ITotal RevenueB + G$29.99 + $1.25 = $31.24
                                                                                      JTotal COGSE + H$9.05 + $0.34 = $9.40
                                                                                      KGross ProfitI − J$31.24 − $9.40 = $21.84
                                                                                      LGross Margin %K ÷ I69.9%
                                                                                      MNet Margin (after OPEX)(K − $1.80) ÷ I($21.84 − $1.80) ÷ $31.24 = 65.6%

                                                                                      Why OPEX is $1.80

                                                                                      The $1.80 figure comes from Tab 1 Section 5 (Operating Cost per User per Month). It bundles payment processing ($1.20 mixed Stripe/Apple IAP), customer support amortized ($0.30), cloud/API ($0.15), SMS/OTP ($0.05), hosting ($0.10). The same number applies across every tier — the assumption being that ops cost scales linearly per active user, regardless of plan size.

                                                                                      3. Per-tier results table (locked numbers)

                                                                                      The full output of Tab 3 — one row per tier, all 7 plans + the Cockpit annual row recomputed to a monthly equivalent.

                                                                                      TierRevenueGB ConsumedeSIM COGSRefuel NetTotal RevTotal COGSGross ProfitGross MarginNet Margin
                                                                                      Economy (PAYG)$4.991.0$1.34$0.00$4.99$1.34$3.6573.1%36.0%
                                                                                      Roster Bundle$19.955.0$6.71$0.37$20.45$6.84$13.6066.5%59.9%
                                                                                      Premium Economy$17.994.0$5.37$0.73$18.99$5.64$13.3570.3%63.2%
                                                                                      Business ⭐$29.996.75$9.06$0.91$31.24$9.40$21.8469.9%65.6%
                                                                                      First$39.9913.5$18.12$1.46$41.99$18.66$23.3355.5%52.3%
                                                                                      First Suite$49.9913.2$17.72$0.73$50.99$17.99$33.0064.7%62.1%
                                                                                      Cockpit (annual → monthly)$24.927.2$9.66$0.55$25.67$9.87$15.8061.6%56.3%
                                                                                      The hero tier: First Suite — $33.00 gross profit per user per month, highest absolute profit on the entire ladder. Customers who upgrade from Business to First Suite are worth an extra $11.18/user/month in profit.

                                                                                      4. Strategic insights

                                                                                      4.1 First Suite is the hero

                                                                                      At $33.00 gross profit / user / month, First Suite generates more absolute profit than any other tier — beating even Cockpit's annual prepay on a monthly-equivalent basis. The reason is structural: First Suite has the same friction-capped consumption as First (~13 GB) but a $10 higher retail price. The pool went from 25 GB to 40 GB on paper, but actual GB delivered stayed flat. Pool expansion is free; price expansion is profit.

                                                                                      4.2 Business is the default RECOMMENDED tier

                                                                                      Business sits at the sweet spot: 70% gross margin, $21.84 profit per user, the highest absolute profit among the broad-market tiers. It's the "everyone should buy this" tier on the price card — high enough that ARPU is meaningful, low enough that broad crew demographics can afford it. This is why it carries the RECOMMENDED flag in the app.

                                                                                      4.3 First is the weakest tier on margin

                                                                                      First's net margin is just 52.3% — the lowest of any subscription tier. The reason: heavy users on First push consumption to 13.5 GB (54% of the 25 GB pool), and at $1.34/GB blended that's $18+ of COGS against just $39.99 revenue. First's job is positional — it bridges Business to First Suite on the price ladder.

                                                                                      First is the "ladder rung" tier. Its purpose is to make First Suite look reasonable. We accept thinner margins here because it pulls Business buyers up.

                                                                                      4.4 Economy is a volume play

                                                                                      At $3.65 gross profit per top-up, Economy needs 2.5+ purchases per month to compete with even the cheapest subscription tier. A user who buys 2 top-ups in a month delivers $7.30 — less than half of Premium Economy. The strategic role of Economy is twofold: (1) acquisition — a $4.99 try-it price has near-zero friction, and (2) upsell anchor — once users buy 3 top-ups in a month ($14.97), they realize Premium Economy ($17.99 for 10 GB) is a better deal and convert.

                                                                                      4.5 Cockpit is about cash flow, not per-user max profit

                                                                                      At $25.67 monthly-equivalent revenue and $15.80 gross profit, Cockpit underperforms Business ($21.84) and First Suite ($33.00) on a per-user-per-month basis. That's by design. Cockpit's value is $299 collected upfront on day 1 — strong cash flow, zero churn for 12 months, predictable annual revenue stream. The annual lock-in matters more than per-month margin maximization.

                                                                                      4.6 The upgrade arithmetic

                                                                                      Upgrade pathProfit deltaAnnual delta per user
                                                                                      Economy → Premium Economy+$9.70/mo+$116/yr
                                                                                      Premium Economy → Business+$8.49/mo+$102/yr
                                                                                      Business → First+$1.49/mo+$18/yr (weak)
                                                                                      Business → First Suite+$11.18/mo+$134/yr
                                                                                      First → First Suite+$9.67/mo+$116/yr

                                                                                      Implication: the strongest in-app upgrade prompt to design is Business → First Suite, skipping First entirely. Marketing should funnel Business users directly to First Suite, not nudge them through First.

                                                                                      5. Downstream consumption — how Tab 3 feeds the rest

                                                                                      Tab 3 is the per-user math factory. Every scaling tab downstream multiplies these per-user numbers by user counts, lifetime, or growth curves.

                                                                                      Downstream tabWhat it does with Tab 3Output
                                                                                      Tab 5 — Volume ScenariosPer-user gross profit × user counts (1K / 5K / 10K / 100K)Monthly P&L at each scale
                                                                                      Tab 6 — 24-Month RolloutPer-user × monthly growth curve24-month revenue + profit projection
                                                                                      Tab 8 — LTV-CAC + ChurnPer-user gross profit × expected lifetime (1 / churn)LTV per tier; LTV/CAC ratio
                                                                                      Tab 10 — Carryover LiabilityConnected via Tab 2's GB Consumed → unused → deferred breakageCarryover aging schedule
                                                                                      Tab 11 — Strategic ScenariosRe-runs per-tier economics under wholesale supplier vs direct supplier pathsStrategic supplier comparison
                                                                                      Tab 12 — Cash + SensitivityPer-user × scenarios × cash conversion timingCash flow + runway sensitivity
                                                                                      Change ANY single number in Tab 3 — wholesale $/GB, OPEX, refuel attach — and the entire downstream P&L cascades. That's why every Tab 3 input is sourced from Tab 1 or Tab 2, never hardcoded here.

                                                                                      8. Bite 6 — Sensitivity analysis (what could break us)

                                                                                      Five "what if" scenarios stress-testing the model. Each shows per-user impact and at-scale dollar consequences.

                                                                                      Scenario 1 — Consumption % rises (users eat more)

                                                                                      If Premium Economy consumption goes 40% → 50%:

                                                                                      MetricNow (40%)If 50%Δ per user
                                                                                      GB Consumed4 GB5 GB+1 GB
                                                                                      Wholesale COGS$5.36$6.70+$1.34
                                                                                      Gross Profit$13.35$12.01−$1.34/user
                                                                                      At 100K users × 13% Premium−$20,904/year

                                                                                      Scenario 2 — Refuel attach drops

                                                                                      If Business refuel attach goes 25% → 10%:

                                                                                      MetricNow (25%)If 10%Δ per user
                                                                                      Refuel Revenue$1.25$0.50−$0.75
                                                                                      Refuel net profit$0.91$0.37−$0.54/user
                                                                                      At 100K users × 8% Business−$5,184/year

                                                                                      Scenario 3 — Wholesale supplier raises prices (the big one)

                                                                                      If blended wholesale rises $1.34 → $2.00 (50% supplier hike):

                                                                                      TierProfit now ($1.34)Profit at $2.00Δ margin
                                                                                      Premium$13.35 (70%)$10.95 (58%)−12 pts
                                                                                      Business$21.84 (70%)$17.39 (56%)−14 pts
                                                                                      First$23.33 (56%)$14.43 (34%)−22 pts ⚠
                                                                                      First Suite$33.00 (65%)$24.29 (48%)−17 pts

                                                                                      Insight: First gets crushed if wholesale rises. Strong argument for moving direct to eSIM Access supplier at scale.

                                                                                      Scenario 4 — Mix shift toward heavy tiers

                                                                                      If First grows from 3% → 6% of users:

                                                                                      MetricAt 3% FirstAt 6% FirstΔ annual
                                                                                      First tier contribution at 100K users$70,080$140,160+$70,080/yr

                                                                                      Net positive on revenue, but First has the lowest margin (56%) — blended margin will dip.

                                                                                      Scenario 5 — Price war / Premium drop

                                                                                      If we drop Premium from $17.99 → $14.99:

                                                                                      Metric$17.99$14.99Δ
                                                                                      Gross profit/user$13.35$10.35−$3.00
                                                                                      Volume increase needed to break even—+29%To match dollar profit

                                                                                      Insight: Premium is fragile to price drops. Don't promo Premium — promo Roster Bundle or Business instead.

                                                                                      Response playbook

                                                                                      RiskIf it materializes — what we do
                                                                                      Consumption risesAccept thinner margins OR pull friction levers harder
                                                                                      Refuel attach dropsMarketing push for top-ups + consider raising refuel price slightly
                                                                                      Wholesale risesAccelerate move to direct eSIM Access supplier — biggest single risk
                                                                                      Mix shifts heavyPush First Suite over First (better margin on heavy tier)
                                                                                      Price war / discount pressureDon't drop Premium — drop Roster Bundle which has more breakage cushion
                                                                                      Bite 6 = "what could break us, and how to respond." The business stays profitable under every single-variable downside — only combined downsides erode margin meaningfully.

                                                                                      The full blueprint for Volume Scenarios lives in a standalone document.                                                                                       Key findings from the Tab 14 discussion (2026-06-02):
                                                                                      • $12.48 blended profit/user verified: 50% Economy x $9.13 + 18% Roster x $13.62 + 13% Premium x $13.36 + 8% Business x $21.86 + 3% First x $28.05 + 2% Suite x $33.03 + 3% Cockpit x $15.82 = $12.48
                                                                                      • Model holds $12.48 flat across all scenarios (conservative). Realistic tier evolution adds $3.2M/yr at 100K users.
                                                                                      • Nudge #1 (after 3rd refuel, trigger Economy to Premium) is the single highest-leverage product feature. Ship at v1.0.
                                                                                      • 5K to 20K users = multi-airline pivot. Emirates ceiling ~5,500 at 25% penetration. Beyond that requires Etihad, JAL, ANA.
                                                                                      • OPEX = $0 real today. $1.80/user/mo in the model is a placeholder. Gross profit = net profit at launch.

                                                                                      PART V — Tab 21: Strategic Scenarios

                                                                                      Tab 21 runs three forward-looking scenarios. Section 3 (Competitive Floor) is the urgent one — it tells us exactly how low we can price before any tier loses money. Economy is the only exposed tier ($0.28 cushion). All subscription tiers are well-defended. Our strategy: compete on the 8-feature bundle, not on price.

                                                                                      Open Tab 21 Visualizer ↗ Open Tab 21 Blueprint ↗
                                                                                      Key findings from the Tab 21 discussion (2026-06-02):
                                                                                      • Sections 1 (wholesale triggers) and 2 (multi-airline) are parked — Year 2+ planning. Section 3 (competitive floor) is relevant NOW.
                                                                                      • Economy floor: $4.71 (COGS $3.36 + OPEX $1.35). Crew SIM reference: $4.99. Cushion: $0.28. This is the only vulnerable tier.
                                                                                      • All subscription tiers have $6–$27 cushion. Roster Bundle: $26.94. First: $25.22. No defensive price moves needed on subscriptions.
                                                                                      • The 8-feature moat (CrewLink, gifting, UAE redemption, Crew Recs, same-SIM, 60% savings, AI support, Cockpit annual) means we compete on bundle — not price.
                                                                                      • 4-step playbook: watch (Days 1-7) → assess impact (Week 2-4) → Spring Promotion only if signups drop → targeted retention for at-risk users.
                                                                                      • Open item: Akito to validate First Suite competitor price (Crew SIM $45 is a placeholder — they have no equivalent tier).

                                                                                      PART VI — Tab 19: Per-Tier Geo Mix

                                                                                      The flat $1.34/GB blended assumption breaks down at the tier level. Each plan tier self-selects users who fly different routes. Economy users vacation in Las Vegas ($4.08/GB). Roster Bundle crew fly Mumbai layovers ($1.37/GB). The 3x cost swing on the same service makes route mix the hidden P&L driver.

                                                                                      Open Tab 19 Visualizer ↗ Open Tab 19 Blueprint ↗
                                                                                      Key findings from the Tab 19 discussion (2026-06-02):
                                                                                      • Economy gross margin at real geo mix: 18.3% ($2.29 net). Default model shows 73%+ — a wildly optimistic assumption when 40% of Economy data is consumed in USA/Tier-C.
                                                                                      • Roster Bundle holds strong: 65.7% gross margin at $1.37/GB blended. Crew flying Mumbai and Bangkok are cheap to serve.
                                                                                      • Maya vs Yuki: same eSIM service. Maya (Economy, Vegas) nets $2.29. Yuki (Roster Bundle, Mumbai) nets $13.10. Same supplier. 5.7x profit gap purely from WHERE they roam.
                                                                                      • Three scenarios: Optimistic (75/20/5 = $1.34), Realistic (40/40/20 = $2.60), Pessimistic (30/35/35 = $3.84). Model default = Optimistic. Real mix is likely Realistic.
                                                                                      • Akito task: validate Tier-A mix with 5–10 crew layover cities. Distinguish real layovers (18+ hours) from turnarounds (1–3 hours, no data usage).

                                                                                      PART VII — Tab 22: Cash + Sensitivity

                                                                                      Three short but critical analyses: Refuel attach sensitivity ($912/mo swing at 1K users from 5% to 30%), failed-eSIM true cost ($10.80 corrected, not $4.00 raw), and the Cockpit cash advantage as a self-funding mechanism. The original Cockpit sheet calculation was buggy — fix applied and documented.

                                                                                      Open Tab 22 Visualizer ↗ Open Tab 22 Blueprint ↗
                                                                                      Key findings from the Tab 22 discussion (2026-06-02):
                                                                                      • Refuel attach breakeven = 15%. At 20%+ it's additive profit. Target 20–25% with a persistent low-data CTA in the app.
                                                                                      • Failed-eSIM true cost = ~$10.80 blended (not $4.00 raw sheet). Our policy is GB credit goodwill, not cash. 70% of failures preventable with device check + in-app QR scanner + AI support agent.
                                                                                      • Cockpit cash bug: original sheet compared annual revenue totals (meaningless). Fix: D = C/2 (average float held during the year). E = D × 4% (money-market interest).
                                                                                      • At 100 Cockpit users: $14,950 extra working capital + $598/yr interest. At 1,000: $149,500 + $5,980/yr. For self-funded business, this is runway without a bridge loan.
                                                                                      • Strategic recommendation: push Cockpit aggressively from day one. It's not just a revenue play — it's a cash flow strategy that reduces founder injection need.

                                                                                      PART VIII — Tab 4: Pricing Simulator

                                                                                      Tab 4 is parked Year-2 reference material. It answers: at any given wholesale cost, what retail price produces a target margin? The key insight: supplier negotiation unlocks +$28K/mo extra margin at 5K users with zero retail price change. Don't touch retail prices to acquire users. Build volume, then negotiate.

                                                                                      Open Tab 4 Visualizer ↗ Open Tab 4 Blueprint ↗
                                                                                      Key findings from the Tab 4 discussion (2026-06-02):
                                                                                      • Current rate $1.34/GB blended (75/20/5 geo mix) is verified. Target $0.30/GB and ceiling $0.20/GB are theoretical estimates, not supplier quotes.
                                                                                      • Aiko on Premium at $1.34/GB: $5.36 COGS, $17.99 retail, 70% margin. At $0.30/GB: $1.20 COGS, same $17.99 retail, 93% margin. +$4.16/user/month, zero retail change.
                                                                                      • Blended savings across tier mix at $0.30/GB target: ~$5.56/user/month. At 5K users = +$27,800/mo. At 100K users = +$556K/mo.
                                                                                      • 4 trigger conditions before this tab becomes active: ~5K users, alternative supplier identified, supplier meeting scheduled, actual quoted rate received.
                                                                                      • Don't use this tab to justify promotional price drops. Margin loss from discounting is certain; user growth is not. The model never recovers below $17.99 Premium.

                                                                                      PART IX — Tab 13: Costs & Burn

                                                                                      Tab 13 is a cost tracking template. As of 2026-06-02, Balraj has spent $0 on the business. The $11K/mo OPEX placeholder in the model is fictional. At $0 OPEX, gross profit equals net profit from the first sale. The Cockpit annual prepay creates $14,950 in working capital at 100 users — this business is self-funding before it spends a dollar.

                                                                                      Open Tab 13 Visualizer ↗ Open Tab 13 Blueprint ↗
                                                                                      Key findings from the Tab 13 discussion (2026-06-02):
                                                                                      • $0 actual spend as of 2026-06-02. The $11K/mo OPEX is a placeholder. Deleting it changes the breakeven from Month 11-12 to Month 1.
                                                                                      • Real Year 1 OPEX estimate: ~$1,800-2,500 (LLC $140 + agent $600/yr + Vivek $600/yr + Apple $99/yr + Google Play $25 + domains ~$50 + optional legal ~$300).
                                                                                      • Cockpit prepay float: $14,950 working capital at 100 users, $149,500 at 1,000 users. Earns $598-$5,980/yr at 4% money market in Mercury.
                                                                                      • Accounting stack: Wave (free) for Year 1. Upgrade to QuickBooks ($30/mo) when revenue exceeds $50K/yr. Monthly close = 1 hour maximum.
                                                                                      • This business may never need outside capital. No developer payroll, no marketing budget, no servers. Every first sale is profitable. Cockpit float covers all Year 1 OPEX many times over.

                                                                                      2026-05-24
                                                                                      Plan tier naming locked — Economy / Premium Economy / Business / First / Cockpit / Refuel プランティア名称確定 — エコノミー / プレミアムエコノミー / ビジネス / ファースト / コックピット / リフューエル
                                                                                      Aviation cabin-class metaphor for self-segmentation. Economy = one-time trip ($3-7). Premium Economy = monthly ($24, 10 GB). Business = monthly ($34, 15 GB). First = monthly ($44, 20 GB). Cockpit = annual ($249, you're in control). Roster Bundle = auto-priced from uploaded roster. Refuel = top-ups ($1.99-2.99/GB). Crew instantly recognize these from their job. 自己セグメンテーションのための航空キャビンクラスメタファー。エコノミー = 1回の旅行（$3-7）。プレミアムエコノミー = 月額（$24、10 GB）。ビジネス = 月額（$34、15 GB）。ファースト = 月額（$44、20 GB）。コックピット = 年間（$249、あなたがコントロール）。ロスターバンドル = ロスターから自動価格設定。リフューエル = トップアップ（$1.99-2.99/GB）。乗務員が自分の仕事から即座に認識できる名称。

                                                                                      UAE market strategy — 4-stage Emirates-first plan (TDRA-aware) UAE 市場戦略 — 4段階エミレーツ優先プラン（TDRA 対応）
                                                                                      Confirmed sequence: Stage 1 = Emirates DXB crew only, word-of-mouth, zero UAE press, target 1K users. Stage 2 = scale to 10K within Emirates (still no UAE press), closed-network verification, app-only distribution. Stage 3 = JAL + ANA expansion (Akito-led). Stage 4 = buy UAE TDRA license at 10K+ users or partner via Etisalat/du white-label. Lesson driver: Airalo was silently network-blocked by TDRA in July 2024 — Delaware incorporation does NOT protect against geographic blocking. 確定したシーケンス:ステージ1 = エミレーツ DXB ベース乗務員のみ、口コミ拡散、UAE プレス露出ゼロ、目標 1,000 ユーザー。ステージ2 = エミレーツ内で 1 万ユーザーまで拡大（UAE プレス露出は引き続きゼロ）、クローズドネットワーク認証、アプリ専用配信。ステージ3 = JAL + ANA 展開（Akito リード）。ステージ4 = 1 万ユーザー超で UAE TDRA ライセンス取得、または Etisalat / du とのホワイトラベル提携。判断トリガー:2024 年 7 月に Airalo が TDRA により事前告知なしにネットワーク ブロックされた事案 — デラウェア法人化は地理的ブロッキングを防がない。

                                                                                      LLC structure — Multi-member (partnership, Form 1065) LLC 構造 — マルチメンバー（パートナーシップ、Form 1065）
                                                                                      Both founders are legal co-owners of the Delaware LLC. IRS treats as partnership — files Form 1065 + K-1s annually (NOT Form 5472 + 1120, which is single-member only). Both members need US ITIN. 両創業者がデラウェア LLC の正式な共同所有者。IRS はパートナーシップとして扱い、Form 1065 + K-1 を毎年提出（Form 5472 + 1120 はシングルメンバー専用のため不適用）。両メンバーとも米国 ITIN が必要。

Demographic mix per recruitment brief (Indian/Subcontinent 9, UK/AU/EU 5-6, Egyptian/Arab 4, Filipino 3, etc.). Beta perk: ongoing discount + 'ambassador' status. Goal: turn each into a referral source. ベータ = Akito のネットワークから手選した Emirates 乗務員 30 名。リクルートメント ブリーフに沿った人口構成（インド系・南アジア 9 名、英・豪・欧 5-6 名、エジプト・アラブ 4 名、フィリピン 3 名 等）。特典: 継続割引 + 『アンバサダー』ステータス。目標: 各人をリファラル源化。

                                                                                      TDRA blocking risk — MED-HIGH (upgraded 2026-05-25) TDRA ブロック リスク — 中〜高（2026-05-25 にレベル上げ）
                                                                                      Airalo was network-blocked by TDRA in April 2024 — still blocked as of 2026-05-25, no appeal channel. Now the #1 mitigation is the WiFi pre-download pattern (download eSIM profile BEFORE entering UAE network), plus supplier diversification (Item 20). Risk likelihood upgraded from Low to MED-HIGH in the risk register. See Phase 0 Item 13 Sub-decision 6 + Phase 1 Item 20 + Phase 3 pre-emption pattern. Airalo は 2024 年 4 月に TDRA によりネットワーク ブロックされた — 2026-05-25 時点で依然ブロック中、異議申し立て手段なし。最大の緩和策は WiFi プリダウンロードパターン（UAE 入国前に eSIM プロファイルをダウンロード）+ サプライヤー多様化（Item 20）。リスク発生確率を「低」から「中〜高」に上方修正。Phase 0 Item 13 サブ判断 6 + Phase 1 Item 20 + Phase 3 プリエンプション パターン参照。
